  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8809862d-1b20-442e-8e33-6b9b51f96528'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6984027525852061789">There’s no such thing as safe in a city at war, a city overrun with monsters. In this dark urban fantasy from author Victoria Schwab<em>, </em>a young woman and a young man must choose whether to become heroes or villains—and friends or enemies—with the future of their home at stake. The first of two books.<br/><br/>Kate Harker and August Flynn are the heirs to a divided city—a city where th</span>
  <span id="freeText6984027525852061789" style="display:none">There’s no such thing as safe in a city at war, a city overrun with monsters. In this dark urban fantasy from author Victoria Schwab<em>, </em>a young woman and a young man must choose whether to become heroes or villains—and friends or enemies—with the future of their home at stake. The first of two books.<br /><br />Kate Harker and August Flynn are the heirs to a divided city—a city where the violence has begun to breed actual monsters. All Kate wants is to be as ruthless as her father, who lets the monsters roam free and makes the humans pay for his protection. All August wants is to be human, as good-hearted as his own father, to play a bigger role in protecting the innocent—but he’s one of the monsters. One who can steal a soul with a simple strain of music. When the chance arises to keep an eye on Kate, who’s just been kicked out of her sixth boarding school and returned home, August jumps at it. But Kate discovers August’s secret, and after a failed assassination attempt the pair must flee for their lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6984027525852061789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_415').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1138398571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138398571" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138398571?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062380852" href="/book/show/26074170-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138398571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10061097389576730504"><blockquote>
  <i>She liked the idea that there were a hundred different Kates, living a hundred different lives. <br/>Maybe in one of them, there were no monsters.</i>
</blockquote><br/>3 1/2 stars. Okay, listen: <b>I feel like I shouldn't like this book</b>. Compare this world to the marvelous multiple Londons, crossdressing pirates and evil twin rulers of the author's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_' title='A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a>, and hell, does it pale in comparison. But screw it - this was dark, monstrous fun!<br/> <br/>Thing is, there are those books you read and you know they are good</span>
  <span id="freeText10061097389576730504" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She liked the idea that there were a hundred different Kates, living a hundred different lives. <br />Maybe in one of them, there were no monsters.</i>
</blockquote><br />3 1/2 stars. Okay, listen: <b>I feel like I shouldn't like this book</b>. Compare this world to the marvelous multiple Londons, crossdressing pirates and evil twin rulers of the author's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>, and hell, does it pale in comparison. But screw it - this was dark, monstrous fun!<br /> <br />Thing is, there are those books you read and you know they are good in an objective way (or as close as is possible). You can't help but <i>appreciate</i> them. <i>This author is way smarter than me</i>, you think. But that's it. You don't stay up late reading chapter after chapter because you need to know what happens. You don't really <i>care</i>.<br /><br />And then there are those books you know are not actually that amazing. The writing is decent, the world is not that unique, but <b>you just can't put them down</b>. That's the difference between a good book and an enjoyable one. For me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> was the latter - a pageturning paranormal thriller with creepy monster rhymes, betrayals and an evil cliffhanger at the end of most of the chapters (I both love and hate when authors do that - <b>don't they understand I need to sleep?!</b>)<br /><br />Yes, this is a world of monsters: the flesh-eating Corsai, the blood-drinking Malchai, and the rarest, most mysterious of all: the soul-stealing Sunai.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Corsai, Corsai, tooth and claw,<br />Shadow and bone will eat you raw.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Classic horror movies have made my skin instantly crawl at those creepy rhymes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[my old favourite being <i>"One, two, Freddie's coming for you; three, four, better lock your door..."</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. In fact, I found parts of this book really scary. Schwab writes some tense scenes, the terror rising in the darkness as the situation grows more hopeless and the monsters creep ever closer (did I mention I need sleep?!). Damn, it was <b>thrilling</b>.<br /><br />Yes, I realize I'm saying more about how this book made me <i>feel</i>, not what actually happens. Probably because, like I said at the beginning, the story and world don't sound that unique. The monsters part is interesting, but it bugs me that this book has some dystopian aspects - it really should have just been a paranormal novel, instead of painting in some vague dysto-US background (this + the male/female perspectives + brewing social unrest = <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> by Marie Lu?). <br /><br />Fortunately, I liked both characters and the third-person narrative; I also liked that the book had a male and a female protagonist but with <b>no romance</b>. I liked the ending (a nice wrap-up with a little bit of evil to keep us waiting for the next installment). I liked that I didn't see some things coming, and I thought it was a testament to the author's characterization that I was really affected by something that happened to a minor character.<br /><br />But mostly? I liked the storytelling. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> won't be winning any originality awards. It won't change the world, or even the face of YA. But it was compelling, intriguing and just the right amount of creepy. I need the second book.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10061097389576730504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11516403451871670632">ETA: I just did my final, final read-through of this book, and I have to say, it was a messy road, and a long revision, but I am really freaking proud of the result. <br/><br/><br/><br/>ETA: IT HAS A COVER!! <br/><br/><br/><br/>Sin City PLUS Romeo and Juliet MINUS romance PLUS monsters.<br/><br/>This is the strangest book I've ever written. I love it. <br/><br/>It's the story of two teens in a broken world, where violent acts breed actual monsters. Some are shadows with teeth that feed on flesh and bone. Some are corpses that feed on blood. And some can </span>
  <span id="freeText11516403451871670632" style="display:none">ETA: I just did my final, final read-through of this book, and I have to say, it was a messy road, and a long revision, but I am really freaking proud of the result. <br /><br /><br /><br />ETA: IT HAS A COVER!! <br /><br /><br /><br />Sin City PLUS Romeo and Juliet MINUS romance PLUS monsters.<br /><br />This is the strangest book I've ever written. I love it. <br /><br />It's the story of two teens in a broken world, where violent acts breed actual monsters. Some are shadows with teeth that feed on flesh and bone. Some are corpses that feed on blood. And some can pass for human. Those feed on souls. <br /><br />It's the story of Kate Harker, the only daughter of a crime boss, and August Flynn, the son of a man trying to hold his city together. She's a human who wants to be a monster, and he's a monster who wishes he were human.<br /><br />It's dark, and violent, and existential, and the whole thing was inspired by a line from VICIOUS: <br /><br />"Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human." <br /><br /><br />8.3.15: EDITED TO ADD: And the official title is...THIS SAVAGE SONG. Why song?<br />Remember when I said that August was a monster? He’s not just any kind of monster, but one of only three soul-eaters in the city. And these rare creatures (he wouldn’t like that word) use music to bring the souls of their prey to surface. <br /><br />But it’s more than that. This book isn’t a solo. It’s a duet. A song played by two very different teens trying to survive a very broken world. There are moments of discord, and a few of harmony, and through it all, they have to keep the melody alive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11516403451871670632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1071485163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1071485163" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1071485163?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062380876" href="/book/show/23299512-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1071485163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7313525245229896790">For a book with such an epic setting, this one is <b>quite generic.</b> The setting is pretty awesome, I mean, imagine a post-apocalyptic world where monsters roam free.<blockquote>
  <i>“Corsai, Corsai, tooth and claw,<br/>Shadow and bone will eat you raw.<br/>Malchai, Malchai, sharp and sly,<br/>Smile and bite and drink you dry.”<br/>“Sunai, Sunai, eyes like coal,<br/>Sing you a song and steal your soul.”</i>
</blockquote>Hell, one of our protagonists is a monster himself. But outside of the setting itself, I found this book <b>emotionless and just...rather d</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7313525245229896790" style="display:none">For a book with such an epic setting, this one is <b>quite generic.</b> The setting is pretty awesome, I mean, imagine a post-apocalyptic world where monsters roam free.<blockquote>
  <i>“Corsai, Corsai, tooth and claw,<br />Shadow and bone will eat you raw.<br />Malchai, Malchai, sharp and sly,<br />Smile and bite and drink you dry.”<br />“Sunai, Sunai, eyes like coal,<br />Sing you a song and steal your soul.”</i>
</blockquote>Hell, one of our protagonists is a monster himself. But outside of the setting itself, I found this book <b>emotionless and just...rather dull.</b><br /><br />First, the main character. Kate Flynn. Insert cookie-cutter-YA-bad-ass-chick here. Me, I would call her <b>a bitch.</b> There is a difference between a strong, fierce female character, and one who is a rebellious jerk just for the sake of being one. I disliked her from the first page, as she ruthlessly set fire to a school run by nuns for the grand, noble reason of "I don't want to be here."<blockquote>
  <i>The night Kate Harker decided to burn down the school chapel, she wasn’t angry or drunk. She was desperate.<br />Burning down the church was really a last resort; she’d already broken a girl’s nose, smoked in the dormitories, cheated on her first exam, and verbally harassed three of the nuns.</i>
</blockquote>Yeah. No. I want a character with inner strength. I don't want a character who does whatever the fuck she wants just to get her own way.<br /><br />The male character isn't all that great either. He's one of those emo, martyred, tortured souls that one seems to find sooooooooooo wonderful and <i>so poetic</i> *sigh* and love so much when one is 12 years old. Then one grows up and realize that hearing your partner whine about how his life sucks all the time is stupid and depressing as fuck. <br /><br />Honestly, I felt like both of the characters had no personality at all. A well-written character rises from the paper, make me feel connected to them, make me feeeeeeeeeeeel things (JON SNOW!!!!!!!!!). These characters are just flat.<br /><br />The storytelling was not to my tastes. I have not read Schwab's books before. I tried reading the acclaimed <i>The Archive</i> and gave up within the first chapters a few years ago. Now I remember why. There is nothing wrong with her writing. It is quite good, in fact, it just doesn't tell a story that interested me. It's not the type of narrative and storytelling that pulled me in. I can only explain this as a matter of book chemistry, and her style of writing did not mesh with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7313525245229896790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2684796021?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785652745" href="/book/show/28696452-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2684796021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7418426943542463070">Taking only 5 ⭐ out of Ilsa's so many and putting them here<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/07/24/this-savage-song-monsters-of-verity-1-by-victoria-schwab/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Plenty of humans are monstrous and plenty of monsters know how to play at being human."</b>
</i> <br/><br/>The synopsis of the book makes me feel like I am being held in a winery basement listening to a dark classical orchestra while in dystopian times and I am not complaining.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>This Savage Song</b>
</i> is the first book of Victoria Schwab’s duology, <i>
  <b>Monsters of Verity</b>
</i>. Probably, I would’ve picked this book u</span>
  <span id="freeText7418426943542463070" style="display:none">Taking only 5 ⭐ out of Ilsa's so many and putting them here<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/07/24/this-savage-song-monsters-of-verity-1-by-victoria-schwab/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><i>
  <b>"Plenty of humans are monstrous and plenty of monsters know how to play at being human."</b>
</i> <br><br>The synopsis of the book makes me feel like I am being held in a winery basement listening to a dark classical orchestra while in dystopian times and I am not complaining.<br><br><i>
  <b>This Savage Song</b>
</i> is the first book of Victoria Schwab’s duology, <i>
  <b>Monsters of Verity</b>
</i>. Probably, I would’ve picked this book up by some point in life and read it, but if it wasn’t for the book club I am part of, probably it would’ve been much later in my life. I would’ve done a huge mistake.<br><br>The concept of the book came to me like a slap on my cheek – I wasn’t expecting <b>any</b> of that. Now I understand why there are so many humans obsessed with Schwab’s works. I get you, people. I get you. It’s okay. I am part of you now. Let us suffer the beauty of Schwab’s mind together. <br><br>The book is so messy and packed with action that I just have to admit that I still didn’t understand it properly, but that didn’t stop me from actually loving it, which is such a hypocrite thing to say, but after all, we don’t understand life either, but we're still living it to the fullest every day, even if we like it or not.<br><br>Now, agreeing that I didn’t understand the book, but I loved it to the fullest, which is a stupid concept but you’ll pardon me for that, let’s get to the part where I explain to you what I <i>felt</i> about it. What <i>got</i> to me.<br><br>The V-City is divided into two sides – the North City and the South City, separated by a truce line called the Seam, each part ruled by another family – in the North, there is Harker; in the South, there is Flynn.<br><br>I liked the way the two rulers were presented – Callum Harker as a true cult leader, cold and ruthless, insensitive, a Godfather in dystopia, and Henry Flynn as a leader of the people, trying to help, trying to prevent, being there to protect, not to attack; kind-hearted and somehow vulnerable.<br><br>The main characters of the book are the children of the two leaders – Kate Harker, a girl who suffered so much in order to find her own way and August Flynn, one of the only three Sunai monsters of the Flynn family.<br><br>There is a whole story about how Kate and August meet and blah. I am not going to talk about that; there’s everything you need to know about that in the book. Instead, I would like to dissect the characters of Kate and August just a bit. And their beautiful friendship. <br><br><i>
  <b>"I don’t want to be a monster"<br>"You’re not," she said, the words automatic, but as she said it, Kate realised that she believed it, too.</b>
</i><br><br>I don’t know and don’t care, but I love Kate and somehow I relate to her badass self, not that I am any of that, but because I also tend to be a bit rude sometimes. What I love most about Kate is her determination to fight until the last breath and her bright mind, restless and ready any time to make connections. She’s a fierce girl, but craving for a soul to be around to, to accept her and tell her she’s enough. She can be confident, but she’s so broken that she only needs someone to reassure her of that. And that someone is August Flynn.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563979222i/27879444._SX540_.jpg" width="346" height="274" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>August Flynn is a weird boy. Maybe because he is not a boy, he’s a monster, but apart from his habit of feeding himself out of sinful souls, to me, he is very human. He’s a thinker. He’s a loner. He’s so weird that he is sweet. But he is strong and he is good and wants to do only good, but the fact that he is what he is, does not always come easy to him. <br><br>I can only see August as a sweet boy, sorry if I do not resonate with your opinions. There is something about him that makes me feel content and make me like him <s>as if he were real</s>. Maybe this is his burning desire to be something else, to be someone he’s not. But, after all, isn’t this a thing we all desire at some point? To be someone we’re not...yet?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563979222i/27879445._SX540_.jpg" width="366" height="254" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, all I can say is that this is the first one of the Schwab’s works that I read and I truly and deeply declare myself a fan. She’s brilliant and her style is mesmerizing. And the idea of the book is something that is just selling it off!<br><br>I love music, everyone does. It has become a thing as necessary in one’s life as air and water. I, for instance, cannot function on a daily basis without listening to music. Because music feels like life itself.<br><br>I cannot help it and I make a very obvious line between this book and my life. Or life in general. Maybe it would come to you a bit cheesy but it’s damn true. And I’d be very curious to find out how many of you actually felt the same way as I did. <br><br><b>I used to make music in order to keep myself on track. I used to make music in order to ease the reality. I used to make music in order to fight my monsters...</b><br><br>...because let’s face it, we all have our own personalised monsters.<br><br>But of course, even monsters can pass as humans. It is only in the eyes of the beholder if you let them be or discard them as beings. <br><br>Ah, and also. In case you are wondering, stop wondering: Callum Harker won the prize for the lamest father in the galaxy. Spread the word.<br><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/7a21034b-9f4a-43a4-9061-7d265d25b631_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>

<div id="review_1070657625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070657625" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070657625?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062380852" href="/book/show/26074170-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-without-romance">ya-without-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070657625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16574849537605348780"><b>REREAD: JUNE 2017</b><br/>Because one must reread the most beautiful and dark and deliciously gorgeously written and most painful books of ever because THAT'S THE BOOKWORM LIFE. No no I'm not that deranged puddle of feels on the floor. That's...someone else.<br/><br/><b>Least to say, this was even better the second time.</b> I am a ball of appreciation for how dark and bloody this book is. And the gorgeous cinnamon perfection that is August, who I still relate to so much. I'm in such thorough appreciation for all his sen</span>
  <span id="freeText16574849537605348780" style="display:none"><b>REREAD: JUNE 2017</b><br />Because one must reread the most beautiful and dark and deliciously gorgeously written and most painful books of ever because THAT'S THE BOOKWORM LIFE. No no I'm not that deranged puddle of feels on the floor. That's...someone else.<br /><br /><b>Least to say, this was even better the second time.</b> I am a ball of appreciation for how dark and bloody this book is. And the gorgeous cinnamon perfection that is August, who I still relate to so much. I'm in such thorough appreciation for all his sensory overload scenes because #so #well #written. <b>I just love him and Kate to death.</b> NOW EXCUSE ME WHILE I GO READ THE SEQUEL (which is finnnnnally mine) AND PROBABLY CONTINUE TO SPIRAL INTO DEEP DARK LOVE FOR SCHWAB'S WORK.<br /><br /><b>Monsters are my favourite.</b><br />(Shh it's normal I swear.)<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ORIGINAL REVIEW: MARCH 2016.</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>This book was MONSTROUSLY pleasing.</b> (Get it?!? Because it's about <i>monsters</i>...so <i>monstrously</i>?!? Okaaaaay I'll stop now.) I'm beginning to think VE Scwab can do no wrong. Although I confess I think her adult books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>) were actually better. BUT THIS WAS STILL SO SO SUFFOCATINGLY GOOD. <br /><br />Where do I even begin?! *screams*<br /><br /><b>First of all: it's about monsters.</b> I loooove monsters. I LOVE 'EM. It's set in this sort of Gotham inspired world, where two forces are waring against each other, and monsters are eating everyone in between. It's mostly human vs monster, but also a fair bit of human vs human. And, naturally, I loved the comparison of <b>the humans being more monsterish than the actual monsters</b>. Gah, I just <i>love</i> that kind of story, okay?!<br /><br />But I will fully confess: <b>I found the first 20% really confusing.</b> That is not good. I actually had to stop reading and <i>go read the blurb</i> and only THEN did the world-building start to make sense. #disappointed <br /><br />And, while we're discussing failings: <b> the story really had VERY little plot.</b> Mostly monsters running around wishing they weren't monster and humans running around being emphatically monstrous. They're trying to avoid wars/stay alive/prove themselves worthy to family... But I honestly <b>expected WAY more, plot-wise.</b><br /><br />OKAY BUT ENOUGH OF THE NEGATIVES. BACK TO WHAT I FREAKING ADORED. Let's talk about the <b>entirely amazing phenomenon that is VE Schwab's writing.</b> Omggg. Can it get anymore divine?!? She has this intensely flawless way of sucking me into the story. I can honestly LOSE TIME reading this writing. And the characters leap off the page, so complex and dimensional and <i>tragic</i>. *suffocates with love* Plus, one thing I was REALLY fond of in this book was the representation of sensory overload. OKAY IT WASN'T REALLY THAT. But, as a person who suffers with sensory overload, when August's monster-melt-downs were described I related so much I wanted to cry. <br /><blockquote>August cringed; the overhead lights were too bright, the scraping of chairs too sharp. Everything was heightened, like the volume on his life was turned up but not in an exciting way. Noises were too loud and smells too strong and pain -- which he <i>did</i> feel -- too sharp. But worse than the senses were the emotions. Agitation and anger burned under his skin and in his head. Every comment and every thought felt like a spark on dry wood.</blockquote><br />If you've ever wondered what it's like to live with sensory overload that happens all. the. freaking. time...THAT. THAT IS IT. DESCRIBED SO EFFORTLESSLY I WANT TO JUST THANK THE BOOKISH HEAVENS THAT IS THIS BOOK.<br /><br /><b>Also the characters were perfect little beasts.</b> I say that with <i>much</i> love, of course. We have two alternate narrators: Kate (a beastly nasty girl who is daughter of a crime-lord and a human) and August (who is a soul-eating monster and adopted-son of the rebels to the crime-lord). August ends up sort of "spying" on Kate at her school and then they get thrown into a run-for-your-life adventure.<br /> • <b>KATE:</b> She was so snarky and bitter and CRUEL but in a really forced way?! Not forced written...forced as in <i>she</i> wanted to be evil but it wasn't really <i>her</i>. IT WAS SO TRAGIC AND SAD. She was awful in order to impress her awful dad. I did love her.<br /> • <b>AUGUST:</b> Omggg, but I loved him <i>more</i>. This is partially because of the sensory-thing. But August is a monster who wishes he wasn't. AND I LOVE THAT KIND OF TROPE. &lt;3 Also he is entirely adorable and sweet and plays violin and I just want to HUG HIM basically. He was tragically beautiful and marvellous and... okay 'scuse me. I am raving. But not even sorry. <br /><br />(But there is...surprisingly...<b>no romance.</b> August and Kate do not ONCE have romantic thoughts towards each other. I am so so SO FREAKING ASTONISHED AND HAPPY. A story of unlikely/forbidden friendship!? HUZZAH.)<br /><br /><b>I'm ever so PLEASED with this book.</b> It was violent and gritty and full of blood. I'm still slightly disappointed in the simplicity of the plot and the ending was wildly open!?!? Not a cliffhanger, but a very very veeery curious call-for-a-sequel. <b>I loved it and I connected to the characters</b> and I had like 9 whole emotions while reading it. A solidly fantastic story I will happily eeeep over eternally.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Monsters, monsters, big and small,<br />they're gonna come and eat you all...</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="16574849537605348780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1604547977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3463908215266542550">I LOVED THIS BOOK. It was totally different from anything I've read before! The world was structured in a very unique way, and both main characters were so likable that reading this book was a pleasure. It was a story that captured me right from the start and held my attention all the way to the end. I went into this novel thinking it would be a clear cut romance, but was surprised to find that signs of it were virtually non-existant! If it develops into a love story in the future, I would be OV</span>
  <span id="freeText3463908215266542550" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK. It was totally different from anything I've read before! The world was structured in a very unique way, and both main characters were so likable that reading this book was a pleasure. It was a story that captured me right from the start and held my attention all the way to the end. I went into this novel thinking it would be a clear cut romance, but was surprised to find that signs of it were virtually non-existant! If it develops into a love story in the future, I would be OVER THE MOON but it was really refreshing to read a book that wasn't built off of a love story. The final few moments of this book were INSANITY, completely unexpected and left me with so many questions for how book two is going to follow up on where things left off. I would recommend this book to ANYONE with a love for fantasy, monsters, dystopian-ish post war settings, strong characters, unique government structure, and a thrilling tale!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1387152387805422993">me @ Victoria ten pages into this, knowing that she’s about to ruin my life and I will enjoy it: <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528702524ra/25717181.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Okay, first of all, let me <s>pretend to</s> care about plot stuff. First of all, this book is <i>so tense</i>. The first half was a managable amount of stress, but during the second half, I was stressing the fuck out in a major way. And second of all, the world is <i>brilliant</i>. I genuinely found this so compelling and interesting - a world in which violence breeds monsters, and those monsters take on the personaliti</span>
  <span id="freeText1387152387805422993" style="display:none">me @ Victoria ten pages into this, knowing that she’s about to ruin my life and I will enjoy it: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528702524ra/25717181.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>Okay, first of all, let me <s>pretend to</s> care about plot stuff. First of all, this book is <i>so tense</i>. The first half was a managable amount of stress, but during the second half, I was stressing the fuck out in a major way. And second of all, the world is <i>brilliant</i>. I genuinely found this so compelling and interesting - a world in which violence breeds monsters, and those monsters take on the personalities of the violence they’ve experienced. <br><br>But come on, let’s get to the main attraction - I want to talk about how fucking great the characters are for a while!! Because the two leads here - and their bro-ship - are literally the most awesome. <br>➽August Flynn - my goddamn fucking son. Clearly dealing with mental illness [on page] and just… written so well, thank you to god and also Jesus and also Victoria Schwab [the lesbian god] for him<br>➽Kate Harker - a badass bitch but also a cinnamon roll. a queen. an icon. an intellectual. she could kill me and I would thank her for it.<br><br>And as for August and Kate’s brotp…………….. It k i l l e d me. A book using a enemies-to-besties platonic friendship as its key dynamic is everything I have ever wanted. <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey/status/998708122276450304" rel="nofollow noopener">This update is my constant everlasting mood.</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Leo could turn a part of himself without losing the whole.<br>Because there was no whole left.<br>Nothing human.”</i>
</blockquote><br>But really, what makes this so great is the fact that the whole book, the entire thing, is based off the monster vs. human conflict. August is a monster who is ashamed of it and wants to be human. Kate is a human who has spent so long attempting to twist herself into something monstrous that she has lost herself. Do you know how much I’m screaming !!!!!!!!<br><br>So, yeah, a ridiculously tense book about two people dealing with their own monster v. human conflicts set in a ridiculously compelling world. <i>This Savage Song</i> was everything I ever wanted and I am so happy I read this.<br><br><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

  <span id="freeText9066052515998217531" style="display:none">These books were still good but I dropped my star ratings and unhauling the hardbacks. I might get them on kindle some day. I just don’t think I’m going to reread them again. <br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾<br><br><b>My July 2016 Owlcrate Box Book! Woot!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470168473i/19897357._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>**MILD SPOILERS**<br><br>I totally loved this book! The idea of the different monsters were really cool. I'm not sure I understand all of it but this is what I understood about the monsters: <br><br>1. Malchai - Drink blood but are not vampires. Formed/Form from murders. <br>2. Corsai - Feed on flesh and bone. Formed/form from violent acts<br>3. Sunai - Feed on sinner souls (killers etc.). Formed/form from major catastrophes (bombs etc.). <br><br>Kate Harker is the daughter of Callum Harker. He controls some of the monsters and he's pretty evil. An event in his life sent him right over the edge. Or maybe he was already on that edge. Kate tries to be evil like her father. She does some some evil things but she's really good deep down inside. <br><br>August Flynn is a sunai and his father (that took him in) is Henry Flynn. He is a good guy trying to keep the bad monsters and people at bay. And trying to keep a peace treaty among said monsters. August also has a brother Leo and sister Ilsa that live with Henry. <br><br>I loved both characters of August and Kate. August is a sweet person that doesn't want to be a monster, but to me he is a good kind of monster. Taking the souls of those that do horrible things isn't so bad. <br><br>Kate is just a bad @ss and gets stuff done. And contrary to what she ever thought, she becomes a monsters friend instead of his enemy. <br><br>Together August and Kate have to fight some enemies that are trying to cause a war. People and things die, things are reborn. <br><br>I thought it was a really cool concept in this new world. I enjoyed learning about the monsters. The story line was awesome and that ending! What is coming next? I need to know! <br><br>Overall the book was awesome, but that's my opinion =) Enjoy <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470309667ra/19912330.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470309667ra/19912331.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Happy Dance for the next book!     <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2428090489?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062380869" href="/book/show/31706495-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2428090489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13628726280407683974">I KEEP TRYING.<br/><br/>I keep picking up V.E. Schwab books, and I just...I don’t <i>get it.</i><br/><br/>I read A Darker Shade of Magic and thought it was meh, but I didn’t have any resounding issues with it and everyone said the sequel was excellent so I figured why not. And then I picked up A Gathering of Shadows and had one of the biggest “what the f*ck?” moments of my lifetime.<br/><br/>But we don’t need to get into that opinion again.<br/><br/>I TBRed A Conjuring of Light anyway. I even bought a copy. I added Vicious to my to-read list</span>
  <span id="freeText13628726280407683974" style="display:none">I KEEP TRYING.<br /><br />I keep picking up V.E. Schwab books, and I just...I don’t <i>get it.</i><br /><br />I read A Darker Shade of Magic and thought it was meh, but I didn’t have any resounding issues with it and everyone said the sequel was excellent so I figured why not. And then I picked up A Gathering of Shadows and had one of the biggest “what the f*ck?” moments of my lifetime.<br /><br />But we don’t need to get into that opinion again.<br /><br />I TBRed A Conjuring of Light anyway. I even bought a copy. I added Vicious to my to-read list, and I bought this book on Book Outlet.<br /><br />And I just wanna know when all my effort is going to pay off. When are good ol’ Victoria and I going to click???<br /><br />This book was fine. The writing was solid -- I’ve never had a problem with her writing. The worldbuilding was good too. It was intricate and fairly wound into the text, neither info dump-y nor overly confusing. Which is rare in worlds this elaborate. Overall, this was creative and pretty well done.<br /><br />But what the hell am I supposed to click with?<br /><br />The characters were fine. They were whatever, really. In fact, they felt only a shade or two off from Kell and Lila of the Shades of Magic series, which makes me wonder whether Schwab really knows how to write characters who aren’t flat, boring young men and spiky, antifeminist-but-trying-to-be-feminist young women.<br /><br />There was no real plot to this, just slowness and then a sudden, out-of-nowhere event that seemed to fit not at all into anything else that had happened. Reading it was occasionally a chore and never entirely pleasant.<br /><br />I didn’t hate this book, but I didn’t even a little bit understand how people love it.<br /><br />Bottom line: I guess I’ll keep trying. But I want a goddamn medal.<br /><br /><br />-------<br />CURRENTLY-READING UPDATE<br /><br />help, i can't stop reading YA fantasy and i don't know who i am anymore</span>
  <a data-text-id="13628726280407683974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1704364604" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1704364604" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1704364604?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062380852" href="/book/show/26074170-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1704364604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5461310978950889841">Man, I feel like I've really knocked it out of the park lately with some fantastic YA reads! I've been trying to balance out my reading schedule with fun reads, alongside ones for review on the blog, and I think this is helping repel the "burnout syndrome". I have no earthly idea why this has been sitting on my physical and digital shelves for so long; I kept meaning to pick it up, but then I would remember the sequel wasn't coming out until the twelfth of never, and other books were shiny or mo</span>
  <span id="freeText5461310978950889841" style="display:none">Man, I feel like I've really knocked it out of the park lately with some fantastic YA reads! I've been trying to balance out my reading schedule with fun reads, alongside ones for review on the blog, and I think this is helping repel the "burnout syndrome". I have no earthly idea why this has been sitting on my physical and digital shelves for so long; I kept meaning to pick it up, but then I would remember the sequel wasn't coming out until the twelfth of never, and other books were shiny or more pressing, and alas, I would reach for a proper book that was more along the lines of required reading. FINALLY! I'm so glad I decided enough was enough; I guess my subconscious was on to something though, since now I don't have to wait long for that gorgeous sequel. Best cover art ever, right?<br /><br />I love how creative the idea behind this plot is. Monsters being created from our transgressions; there's just something so poetic and disturbing about it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> was able to create a high fantasy visual to give us thought into just how our actions, good and bad, can have a ripple effect on the world around us. I found myself easily getting lost in the world of Verity; of course the author, being the writing queen she is, was able to slowly immerse us into this dystopian world without using the dreaded info dump. During the first 100 pages, we are left in the dark about many of the going ons, and we are slowly filled in, which gave me all the tinglies in my suspense-loving bones. I connected immediately with August; while it took awhile to warm up to Kate I found myself very protective over her as we followed alongside the journey. And wow! That ending! What a perfect segue into the final entry. I could have definitely enjoyed this being a full fledged trilogy but I won't be greedy and am grateful for what I can get. :) If you have been living under a rock such as I the past year, please do yourself a favor and pick this one up asap. We can be all caught up and fangirl (or boy) over the next book together as us bookworm creatures do. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5461310978950889841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2452515936" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10157103218015170577">quick! someone alert the vatican because there has been a miracle - i read a book about monsters and i actually enjoyed it!?! <br/><br/>this was my first schwab experience and let me tell you what. i understand the hype, i really do. because the lady can <i>W R I T E</i>. the flow was effortless, the pacing was spot on, and her words were captivating. i just loved the writing style so much. she was able to take a subject that i had no interest in and made me invested in the story - further proof of her talent. <br/><br/>t</span>
  <span id="freeText10157103218015170577" style="display:none">quick! someone alert the vatican because there has been a miracle - i read a book about monsters and i actually enjoyed it!?! <br /><br />this was my first schwab experience and let me tell you what. i understand the hype, i really do. because the lady can <i>W R I T E</i>. the flow was effortless, the pacing was spot on, and her words were captivating. i just loved the writing style so much. she was able to take a subject that i had no interest in and made me invested in the story - further proof of her talent. <br /><br />the story itself was pretty good. i was a little confused at first with all of the world building within the city, and the distinction between monsters, and why there were monsters in the first place. but i just let myself go along for the ride and was pleasantly surprised. mainly because the characters were so well developed - their struggles and personalities and desires felt so relatable and real. august was just too precious for his own good. so even though the plot was a little so-so, the characters and writing definitely made up for it! <br /><br />cant wait to pick up the next book and see what becomes of my little monster. i hope he finds the peace he is looking for. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1424170601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424170601" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424170601?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062380876" href="/book/show/23299512-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424170601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1437588316045242116"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Ya know...<br/><br/>It pains me on a personal level to give a book with such a stunning cover such a low rating, but I cannot deny my problems with it no matter how much I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab' title='V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>V.E. Schwab</a>'s book covers or her writing.<br/><br/>This book has such an <u>intriguing premise.</u><br/><br/>Imagine this:<br/><br/><i>Monsters manifesting into existence as a result of sin. A city literally divided between two leaders, both with their own ideas about how to protect their citizens. Kate, desperately trying to prove her savagery an</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1437588316045242116" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Ya know...<br /><br />It pains me on a personal level to give a book with such a stunning cover such a low rating, but I cannot deny my problems with it no matter how much I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a>'s book covers or her writing.<br /><br />This book has such an <u>intriguing premise.</u><br /><br />Imagine this:<br /><br /><i>Monsters manifesting into existence as a result of sin. A city literally divided between two leaders, both with their own ideas about how to protect their citizens. Kate, desperately trying to prove her savagery and be the devil her father always wanted her to be. August, a Sunai monster, hopelessly clinging to his wish to be human.</i><br /><br />And on top of this badass premise, <b>no fucking love story.</b><br /><br />But for all of those unique elements, this book could not be saved from its own mediocrity. <br /><br />When I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20671290.Vicious" title="Vicious by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>, it really set Schwab apart for me. That story is captivating with dynamic and believable characters.<br /><br />But with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>, I feel as though <i>something</i> is preventing me from getting on board. <br /><br />I appreciate what Schwab sets out to do here. Kate is a cutthroat, stubborn &amp; impulsive. August is quiet and contemplative, a lover of music. These two seem amazing on paper, <b>but for some reason I remain unconvinced.</b><br /><br />I adore their ambitions. It <i>sounds</i> great to have a female lead yearning to be a proper villain. It <i>sounds</i> excellent to have a male lead who is vulnerable and searching for his humanity.<br /><br /><b>But somewhere in the process of breathing life into these characters, Schwab missed the mark.</b><br /><br />No matter how much I wanted to care about these characters, I didn't. I couldn't. They didn't feel real. Even with Schwab's <u>amazing talent for weaving words together</u> I cannot in all good conscience tell you that this book will blow you away.<br /><br />The writing is to die for. Schwab's style is gorgeous and fluid in a way that only a master of writing can achieve. <br /><br />However, the story, the characterization, and unfortunately even the world building <u>will leave you feeling like something crucial is missing.</u><br /><br />I don't know that I'll be continuing on with this series. There were a handful of excellent moments, but whether or not they are enough to salvage my interest will have to wait until June.<br /><br /><i><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/34-mary-s-reviews/452-thissavagesong" rel="nofollow noopener">This review</a> and other reviews of mine can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Nest</a>!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1437588316045242116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1818001908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1818001908" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1818001908?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062380852" href="/book/show/26074170-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way">broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818001908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14488565703622212765"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Monsters, monsters, big and small,<br/>"They're gonna come and eat you all.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>So, I totally wasn’t expecting to love this so much?? I’ve read Schwab’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_' title='A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a> series, and then everything I’d seen suggested this wasn’t as good. But I enjoyed it so much more?? (<i>Sacrilege!</i> I know. I know.)<br/><br/>Something about this <b>dark, egregious atmosphere </b> clawed it’s way into my cold, dead heart. Taking place in an alternate US where the states reconstructed after Vietnam, the story had the potent</span>
  <span id="freeText14488565703622212765" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Monsters, monsters, big and small,<br>"They're gonna come and eat you all.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>So, I totally wasn’t expecting to love this so much?? I’ve read Schwab’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> series, and then everything I’d seen suggested this wasn’t as good. But I enjoyed it so much more?? (<i>Sacrilege!</i> I know. I know.)<br><br>Something about this <b>dark, egregious atmosphere </b> clawed it’s way into my cold, dead heart. Taking place in an alternate US where the states reconstructed after Vietnam, the story had the potential to feel like so many other YA dystopias. But this transcends so much of the cluttered drama? <b>The idea that violence breeds more violence in the form of monstrous creatures</b> is so much more mature and philosophical than <i>“society wants me to be the same!!1! BUt we are all different!!” </i><br><br>(And yes. I’m aware I just said monsters were mature. )<br><br>This book could so easily have spouted a ‘violence is bad. Don’t do it’ it message-- instead <b>this is filled with morally ambiguous characters.</b> Sweet, sensitive August literally has to eat souls to survive and despite his penchant for humanity-- he’s <i>not</i> part of it. But in a world where humans are happy to slaughter each other… should he really be striving for humanity anyway? Instead of a simple misplaced-paranormal creature element, this raises much deeper ethical questions. <b>And there isn’t a simple <i>right</i> answer.</b> It’s not an easy <i>"I’ll feed off animals and be a good vampire" </i> solution, but a struggle for him to find something he can live with. <br><br>Now let me tell y’all about my girl Kate. <b>My aesthetic is blondes with switchblades.</b> The complete antithesis to August, her father leads the North City with no tolerance for weakness. Kate is so desperate to find her place in her father’s city and feel at home, that she’s been systematically trying to get rid of her own humanity. (Homegirl doesn't seem to realize her quest to belong probably counts as being human.) <b>She’s not a good person, but she is relatable.</b> It’s hard to support all of her actions, but her development felt organic and I just loved her. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501413583ra/23455933.gif" width="400" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>In addition to a setting I loved and characters I loved-- I loved this plot.<br><br>Once again, this had the potential to fall back on tropes but instead subverts them and <b>remains unpredictable.</b> Without spoiling, Kate notices August’s weird behavior and <i>trusts her instincts</i>. Please give me more YA heroines who don’t shrug off sketchy behavior. But also, <b>there’s no romance.</b> It would have been <i>so</i> easy for Schwab to go that road, but their individual stories and friendship are enough. <br><br>I understand the complaints however, and completely acknowledge that <b>parts of this are gimmicky.</b> For instance, August’s tally-mark tattoos appear each day he doesn't go "dark." It seemed counterproductive of everything the Sunai are?? Aren’t they supposed to <i>want</i> to go dark?? Why would their bodies be like <i>“good job here’s your sticker for the day”</i> when they don’t? Honestly, I'd have preferred August keeping track of the days himself or the compound or something.<br><br>But the gimmicks were few and completely overshadowed by all the <i>brilliant</i> things? Including Queen Schwab’s mastery with words. It’s just perfect? How does she do it??<br><br><b>Overall:</b><br>RIP Kaylin 1997-2017</span>
  <a data-text-id="14488565703622212765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1374794056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374794056" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374794056?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062380852" href="/book/show/26074170-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374794056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6893449604074592374"><i>"It was a cycle of whimpers and bangs, gruesome beginnings and bloody ends."</i><br/><br/>I've read <i>The Archived</i> and <i> The Unbound</i>. I've read <i> Vicious</i> and <i>The Near Witch</i>, I've read <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> and <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i>.<br/>I've read every YA and Adult Fantasy novel Victoria Schwab has written, and compared to all of them, <i>This Savage Song</i> fell flat.<br/><br/>I love Victoria Schwab. Her writing is stunning, her stories unique, her characters intriguing. <i>This Savage Song</i> had all of this, but much less than her pr</span>
  <span id="freeText6893449604074592374" style="display:none"><i>"It was a cycle of whimpers and bangs, gruesome beginnings and bloody ends."</i><br /><br />I've read <i>The Archived</i> and <i> The Unbound</i>. I've read <i> Vicious</i> and <i>The Near Witch</i>, I've read <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> and <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i>.<br />I've read every YA and Adult Fantasy novel Victoria Schwab has written, and compared to all of them, <i>This Savage Song</i> fell flat.<br /><br />I love Victoria Schwab. Her writing is stunning, her stories unique, her characters intriguing. <i>This Savage Song</i> had all of this, but much less than her previous works.<br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br />This is such a promising story, such an exciting dystopian setting. Monsters and songs, action and thrill. Thing is, I expected a little more. I'm not exactly disappointed, but there's room for more suspense and adventure.<br />I welcomed "Romeo and Juliet minus romance" with open arms. It's great that the stereotypical male plus female protagonists didn't fall in love for once. I don't need romance...but I can't lie that it makes things a little more exciting. Now I'm not sure if one or both of the main characters are asexual, aromantic, pansexual or something completely different. All of them would be great. But a little love in the sequel would spice things up nicely.<br />The story was also slightly predictable, the writing adding to its predictability. Sometimes a little repetitive, I often expected what was coming next and foresaw several smaller and bigger details.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br />Fan of August, not a fan of Kate. While he seems like a sensitive and relatable character, she seems unnecessarily cruel and cold. I'm not exactly sure if Kate is 16 or 18 but she sure is smart enough to differentiate between establishing respect and downright bullying. However big her daddy issues, it's just not cool.<br />Overall I felt like most characters weren't as real and refined as usual. Both of them lacked somewhat in character depth in my opinion.<br /><br />In a nutshell: Great work, but lacking in finesse in several aspects. It just couldn't live up to Schwab's previous works.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6893449604074592374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12972350911879886024" style="display:none">I freaking love the title of this book!<br /><br />3.5 STARS<br /><br /><b>

</b><br /><br />Just want to put it out there, my favorite character wasn't Kate, or August, IT WAS LEO! But i'm not going to talk about the plot or the characters. It's better if you find out yourself. <br /><br />This was a decent read. As always, i enjoyed Victoria's writing, but something was missing. It just wasn't as epic as her other books. I still applaud you, Schwab, for coming up with yet another unique and astonishing story. It's not easy these days. I feel like most books i read have that same old plot, cliche characters, especially in YA. It also could be challenging for an author to write multiple books that aren't similar. Victoria Schwab writes 'em like a pro! Though This Savage Song was just okay, i am super excited about <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener">Our Dark Duet</a>. I saw this more like a prequel. Shit is about to go down. That ending gave me the chills. Can't wait. <br /><br />I've been watching her interviews lately, there is a chance i might be in love with that woman. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3113621483399116764"><i> “It doesn’t matter if you’re monster or human. Living hurts.” </i><br/><br/>Thoroughly enjoyed this one!<br/><br/>In this dystopian version of the United States monsters wreak havoc during the night, and no one is safe. 3 types of monster exist – Malachi, Corsai and Sunai, each are caused by an act of violence from one human to another. Corsai from random acts of violence, Malachi from murder and Sunai from the worst of acts – such as terrorism or mass murder.<br/><br/>August is one such Sunai. Born at age 12, he lives with Hen</span>
  <span id="freeText3113621483399116764" style="display:none"><i> “It doesn’t matter if you’re monster or human. Living hurts.” </i><br /><br />Thoroughly enjoyed this one!<br /><br />In this dystopian version of the United States monsters wreak havoc during the night, and no one is safe. 3 types of monster exist – Malachi, Corsai and Sunai, each are caused by an act of violence from one human to another. Corsai from random acts of violence, Malachi from murder and Sunai from the worst of acts – such as terrorism or mass murder.<br /><br />August is one such Sunai. Born at age 12, he lives with Henry Flynn and 2 other Sunai – his brother Leo and sister Ilsa. The Flynn family control one half of V City, they protect the citizens from Malachi and Corsai, and hold a very precarious truce with the Harker family – the family that control the other half of V City. <br /><br />Kate Harker is the daughter of Callum Harker. His side of V City is controlled by fear, violence and money. Citizens pay for his protection, he gives them a medallion to wear at all times that shows the Monsters they are under his protection, and he keeps the Malachi and Corsai on a tight leash. <br />When August is sent to a normal high school, to keep an eye on Kate Harker in case the truce breaks, he isn’t sure he can do it. Pretending to be human and hiding who he truly is puts him at serious risk. <br /><br />As Kate and August become friends, Kate grows suspicious. What is August hiding? And why?<br />As the secrets unfold and the number of enemies piles up, I was sucked in to this fast paced and exciting urban fantasy; where no one can be trusted – even family. <br />Can’t wait for book 2!<br /><br /><i> “We are not servants. We are not slaves. We are wolves among sheep. Monsters among men…our time is coming.” </i><br /><br /><br /><br />********************<br /><br />After The Shades of Magic trilogy I am excited to read what else Schwab has written!</span>
