  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1960445395?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062380876" href="/book/show/23299512-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960445395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2008638705149817285">I'm between 4.5 and 5 stars, but heck, I'll round up!<br/><br/>So when I finished devouring this book last night before I went to bed, I tried to think of the best way to sum up my feelings. Sometimes when I'm at a loss for words I turn to those more articulate than I am, so:<br/><br/><div>
  <a href='https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-W70AkM1J-YY/WOQ6P_jjqXI/AAAAAAAALwY/jTHbQVv2OAE65okJHG-JioMsT_CQWv5GQCLcB/s1600/oprah.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491354927ra/22401737.gif' width='320' height='172' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/>Ah, thanks, Oprah!<br/><br/>It is a time in the (hopefully very) distant future. At one point, monsters tried to take control of a city. It led to massive destruction, but ultimately a truce was reached which divided the city. One h</span>
  <span id="freeText2008638705149817285" style="display:none">I'm between 4.5 and 5 stars, but heck, I'll round up!<br><br>So when I finished devouring this book last night before I went to bed, I tried to think of the best way to sum up my feelings. Sometimes when I'm at a loss for words I turn to those more articulate than I am, so:<br><br><div>
  <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-W70AkM1J-YY/WOQ6P_jjqXI/AAAAAAAALwY/jTHbQVv2OAE65okJHG-JioMsT_CQWv5GQCLcB/s1600/oprah.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491354927ra/22401737.gif" width="320" height="172" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>Ah, thanks, Oprah!<br><br>It is a time in the (hopefully very) distant future. At one point, monsters tried to take control of a city. It led to massive destruction, but ultimately a truce was reached which divided the city. One half is run by Harker, a ruthless man whose ambition and lust for power are nearly as dangerous as the monsters he allows to roam free, so he can then charge the city's residents for his protection from them. The other half of the city is run by the more noble-minded Flynn, who wants to keep his residents safe by controlling the monsters, not harnessing them as pawns in a shakedown.<br><br>Neither side has complete support, as the truce seems to be weakening. Harker's daughter, Kate, who has gotten herself expelled from her sixth boarding school in five years, has returned home, much to her father's chagrin. She wants to prove that she is just as ruthless as her father, and wants him to finally let her stay with him, and take her under his wing. But she must battle not only her father's ambition and his memories of her late mother, but also the monster he has trained as his second in command.<br><br>When Kate is sent to another school in town, Flynn and his followers jump at the chance to get someone close to her, to watch for signs the truce may be breaking. Flynn's youngest son, August, who wants simply to be kind, to live a good life, is pressed into service. The thing is, August is a monster, the rarest of the three breeds, who can steal a person's soul by playing his violin. He needs to hide his secret from everyone in school, especially Kate, but for the first time in his life, he feels as if he <i>belongs</i>, he starts to make friends, and he is fascinated by Kate's intelligence—until she figures out what he really is.<br><br>When an attempt on Kate's life sends them both fleeing, they must make a truce of their own. August wants only to protect Kate, and Kate wants to live, although she isn't sure if capturing August could be the prize she needs to cement her relationship with her father. As they seek freedom and safety, they still long for the comfort of their families, even as they realize their families may not provide the safe haven they thought. They must fight not only the enemies they expect but enemies they don't, and they face the toughest battle of all—the enemies within themselves.<br><br>Right off the bat, I'll say that obviously this isn't a book for everyone. If you don't like this type of fantasy story, Victoria Schwab's storytelling, no matter how strong a spell she casts, probably won't lure you in. But don't rule it out because you think it's going to be all <b>
  <i>Twilight</i>
</b>-y (a new adjective), because the monsters in this book don't have the Cullenesque shimmer, and more importantly, one of the best things that Schwab does in this book is keep the lovesickness and most of the angstiness out. That makes <b>
  <i>This Savage Song</i>
</b> a much stronger story instead of some YA-ish soap opera.<br><br>I love authors who can take you into another world and immerse you so fully. That's a credit to Schwab's incredible creativity and the imagery she uses. There is a vividness to the pictures she paints, and I'd love to see this made into a movie to see just how closely what I saw in my mind's eye while reading this book hews to the film adaptation. Is it a little overly dramatic at times? Sure. A little predictable? Of course. But it doesn't matter, because the characters she has created fascinated me, flaws and all.<br><br>When you add to your stress level at work by taking a longer lunch than you should so you can keep reading, you know you've found a good book. (Lucky I'm the boss!) When you find yourself taking your glasses off during the NCAA championship so you can race through the remainder of the story before bed, you know you've found a good book. This was tremendously entertaining and well-done, and I'll be all over the sequel when it comes out this summer! <br><br>See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2008638705149817285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Schwab's books. This is the fourth book I've read by her and it did not disappoint. She constantly </span>
  <span id="freeText17725930350007404259" style="display:none">[4.5] REREAD! HOW DID I FORGET THAT ENDING?! MY MEMORY IS THE SHITTEST, I SWEAR! <br /><br />Straight onto Our Dark Duet, though my soul is in agony! August better be getting that redemption he deserves. If Schwab pulls a Holland on him, I'm gonna lose my mind. Hate-mail is what I'll be writing... <br /><br /><br /><b> Initial review:</b><br /><br /><br />[4.5] That ending!! I. Need. More!!!<br /><br />As per usual, I always have the best time reading one of V.E. Schwab's books. This is the fourth book I've read by her and it did not disappoint. She constantly delivers when it comes to her flawless, entrancing and almost graceful-like writing style, the complex, but lovable characters and the unique plot. <br /><br />I don't know why I'm not giving it a 5 stars. I think I can't help but unconsciously compare it to Vicious or the Shades of Magic trilogy — unreasonable, I know — which were perfection for me. Having said that though, I can't as of now, point out a fault or a flaw in this book either. <br /><br />It borders between urban fantasy and dystopia, it was action packed and fast paced, neither was I bored at any point. The world-building was solid as were the characterisation. I just wish it was longer as it left me wanting for more. More pages and more detail, but it makes me ridiculously excited for the next book and to find out what's in store. I want to be surrounded by those characters and be in that world again.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2484487037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484487037" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484487037?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484487037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10629425756709909057"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The beautiful thing about books was that anyone could open them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I did it! I finally read a book by author Victoria Schwab. My journey has finally started and although it wasn't a great start, it doesn't end here. She has so many books published and more are coming up that I need to understand what all the hype is about. My journey actually began when I started reading <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> back in 2016, but I stopped reading it. There's no reason behind it. I really just put my boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10629425756709909057" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The beautiful thing about books was that anyone could open them.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I did it! I finally read a book by author Victoria Schwab. My journey has finally started and although it wasn't a great start, it doesn't end here. She has so many books published and more are coming up that I need to understand what all the hype is about. My journey actually began when I started reading <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> back in 2016, but I stopped reading it. There's no reason behind it. I really just put my bookmark on my page and literally forgot I was reading it that the bookmark soon got covered and I totally had forgotten I was reading it so I put it with my other stack of <i>to read</i> books in a cabinet. Yesterday I opened the book and saw the bookmark on page 145 and was tempted to start reading from there but I really forgot everything about it so I think the best thing to do is start over.<br /><br />I started reading This Savage Song in 2016 as well and put it <i>"on hold"</i> for the longest year ever. I read like 20 pages and gave up because I didn't understand what the hell was happening. It was only the prologue, which I figured was dumb of me because if I couldn't understand the prologue, how was I going to understand the rest? I noticed my ex-best friend loved it and one of my friends kept yelling at me because I DNF'd it at a page that didn't make sense to DNF a book. <b>Although now I regret not finishing it before, I don't regret it as much as I thought I would because, truth be told, this wasn't as great as I thought it would.</b> Don't get me wrong, I can see why some people call Victoria one of the greatest writers because yes, this author can definitely write, but what threw it off for me were that my expectations went down, down, down as I continued flipping pages and the ending overall was not predictable for me since I don't predict, but it could've been better. I mean, one of the things I hate the most in books is leaving everything towards the end. The whole twists and turns happen at 20 pages before the book is over and it is not one of the best experiences I have with books.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It was a game she sometimes played, ever since she learned about the theory of infinite parallels, the idea that a person's path through life wasn't really a line, but a tree, every decision a divergent branch, resulting in a divergent you.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>This Savage Song</i> follows two characters who want to be different than who they are. Kate Harker wants to be even more ruthless than her father even though her father and everyone else doesn't see her as someone worse than him. She wants to prove to him that she can go home and be more than what he wants, even if it means burning a whole chapel or getting expelled from 6 different schools. August Flynn is a monster everyone would fear if they knew his real identity. He wants nothing more than to blend in and <i>be human</i>, even if it means he has to befriend Kate Harker, the heir to the man who is enemies with Flynn and his family. <br /><br />The two are divided in different cities with two different kind of fathers—one protects (or rather, enslaves) monsters and the other kills them. There was a truce that was made for the people to be protected from these monsters that slaughter the whole city but, the truce is weakening, and so is the protection and the guarantee that people will be able to walk in their city without being scared. Truth be told, there never was a guaranteed safe city, just a guaranteed protection at a point. Harker was able to create Medallions that the people carry so the monsters don't get near them, and Flynn has connections with the FTF, the ones who sink these medals into the monsters hearts since that is the only way to kill them. When Kate and August cross paths, there's something about the two that draws one into the other, but as the two begin to form a closer bond, Kate ends up finding out the secret identity of August, and is not sure if she should turn him in to her father so she can prove to him that she is her father's daughter after all, or hide and flee with him, finding out other secrets from her father herself.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Every weakness exposes flesh, and flesh invites a knife.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I don't usually read something like this, but I knew Victoria's writing style and I knew most of her YA books had a form of dark and gritty style, which is why I wanted to finally give this author a chance. She's been praised and hyped by so many of my friends that I felt it was the time I jump on the bandwagon. <br /><br /><b>First things first, I was not the biggest fan of Kate, even though my update for this book may say otherwise.</b> I knew August and Kate wanted to be different than who they were seen as, but I didn't expect it to end that way. I loved Kate's character in the beginning, especially the prologue, but my expectations decreased so much I was then disappointed I had to accept the fact. The prologue where we are introduced to Kate was one of the greatest prologues I had ever read. The way Victoria hooks you into Kate's life and character, you automatically fall in love with her and think she's this really cool character you want to be friends with even though deep down inside you would be scared for your life because she's a hidden ruthless killer. <br /><br />Or well, you thought. <br /><br /><b>To be honest, Kate seemed like she didn't give one fuck about anyone or anything besides herself and I thought that was fucking great!</b> But it didn't end that way, and it didn't continue that way either. When she met August, she actually changed—the way she thought and the way she acted changed and I really hated that. When reading about her, I imagined her to be a ruthless killer because of her being kicked out of her 6 different boarding schools, the chapel burning, the cigarettes she smoked in school, the injury she gave her teacher, the laughter she gave when people made way for her, the incident with Charlotte in the bathroom—it all seemed like she was not weak and instead build upon herself, but instead she built down, and I hated the fact that her ambitions were literally never completed. She's seen as cold and heartless, but we later see who she really is. She was...<i>bland.</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You’re not your father.”<br />Kate tensed imperceptibly at that, then managed to draw her mouth into a small, cruel smile. “Can I tell you a secret?”<br />“Of course,” said Rachel.<br />Kate leaned in and brought her lips to the girl’s ear. “I’m much worse.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />August, <i>oh August,</i> I felt bad for him in the beginning. He was a monster, but he wasn't evil, cruel, and he didn't slaughter innocent lives like the rest. He did it once, and he never wanted to do it again because he couldn't stand the sight of it. He wanted to be different than his brother and sister. He wanted to be someone his father didn't think he couldn't be, someone who would look at him and think of him as human. That's what he wanted, <i>to be human.</i> I didn't have a problem with August and I was quite glad he finally came to accept himself and his identity. <b>He had a tough battle with self-discovery and it took some time, but August was really like anyone else, trying to discover himself and seeing if his characteristics were the features he wanted to show everyone else.</b> He was more calm and sweet, and I felt bad for him even in the end because of how much he had to suffer and endure the pain of not ending the lives of some innocent people. Honestly Victoria better protect this precious boy because he has done nothing wrong in his life to deserve all the pain he went through and if he has to go through more, I won't endure the pain of reading about his endurance. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He wasn't made of flesh and bone, or starlight.<br />He was made of darkness.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Also, I almost forgot to mention my actual favorite side character: <b>Allegro.</b> Look, August truly is such a nice, caring and heart-warming character that truly does not deserve to suffer for at least the one bit. He really took in this kitten because he looked into his eyes and saw that this kitten saw him as someone good and he felt bad because he knew these animals also died if they wandered around at night like humans. Also, bless Ilsa for naming it Allegro because I felt like it really fit him and I don't know, I'm allergic to cats but this cat was really a cute addition to the story.<br /><br /><b>The writing of this author is truly and beautifully captivating.</b> Victoria created beautiful dialogues and world-building that had me imagining how the world of Verity would look like in a big screen. To be honest, I'm not the biggest fan of a book-to-screen trope, but I would love to see this book become a movie. I feel like the whole idea of V-City becoming a true adaption would truly be mesmerizing and one of the most beautiful things, especially since the world-building of Schwab is written in ways where your mind is completely full of it that there's no more room for imaginations. And well, that is if the producers would make the movie like Schwab has written it, since sometimes movies ruin the books because of badly and loosely produced they are.<br /><br />The book is about monsters and surviving them, but we don't see a lot of these monsters, only the common ones that were Harkers or we heard about the ones Leo or August killed. I also wished we got some more information and a backstory of all the characters. To be honest, other than August, I really loved Ilsa's characters and the whole idea of her stars was so interesting to me. I wanted to know more about the Barren, more about what these stars mean to Ilsa and how exactly she got them, and also, why stars? Also, what did Leo have if August had tallies? Maybe it was told, but I probably missed it or skipped it or just really and plainly don't remember. I really just wanted more information of V-City, Kate, August, Kate's mother, her father, Ilsa, and hell even Leo, even though I disliked him quite a lot. The monsters were the reason I was reading this, well, part of the reason other than that it was because its Victoria Schwab and I've had this on hold for like, a year and some months, so I was interested in knowing about these Corsai that eat you raw, Malchai that drink you dry, and Sunai that steal your soul.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Monsters, monsters, big and small,<br />"They're gonna come and eat you all.<br />Corsai, Corsai, tooth and claw,<br />Shadow and bone will eat you raw.<br />Malchai, Malchai, sharp and sly,<br />Smile and bite and drink you dry.<br />Sunai, Sunai, eyes like coal,<br />Sing you a song and steal your soul.<br />Monsters, monsters, big and small,<br />They're gonna come and eat you all!</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Overall, <i>This Savage Song</i> was not the best way to start this journey of Victoria Schwab but I'm really glad she writes differently than other YA authors. The nonphysical friendship between Kate and August with sass and orders being taken and given. The story wasn't creepy, but it was thrilling, making you suspicious and angsty at times. <b>And as previously said, the writing and atmospheric world-building is just stunning.</b> Also, I hope my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/45365270-nadhira-satria" rel="nofollow noopener">Nadhira</a> is finally proud of me for finishing this.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It doesn't matter if you're monster or human. Living hurts.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10629425756709909057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1437808191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437808191" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1437808191?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781785652745" href="/book/show/28696452-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437808191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16952691068445638473"><b>"And you?" asked Kate. "Your brother is righteous, your sister is scattered. What does that make you?"<br/>When August answered, the word was small, almost too quiet to hear. "Lost."</b><br/><br/>This is the fourth of Schwab's books that I read, and I think I finally realized this very incontrovertible truth about the universe, which I believe I summed up adequately enough in the following statement: <b>It's Schwab's, it's good.</b><br/><br/>•First and foremost, as always, <b>the writing</b>. This marvellous, marvellous thing that is Vic</span>
  <span id="freeText16952691068445638473" style="display:none"><b>"And you?" asked Kate. "Your brother is righteous, your sister is scattered. What does that make you?"<br />When August answered, the word was small, almost too quiet to hear. "Lost."</b><br /><br />This is the fourth of Schwab's books that I read, and I think I finally realized this very incontrovertible truth about the universe, which I believe I summed up adequately enough in the following statement: <b>It's Schwab's, it's good.</b><br /><br />•First and foremost, as always, <b>the writing</b>. This marvellous, marvellous thing that is Victoria's writing. She takes storytelling and makes of it something modern and ancient at once: something <b>old</b>, tastefully dusty, elegantly worn; something <b>new</b>, shiny, fashionably casual and unaffected. It's balance, control, then fire and emotion. I do not how she never fails to find this happy medium. It's a <b>state of grace</b>. Bliss. Ink-and-paper-shaped holy spirit. I don't know. I know that it's <b>perfect</b>, I know that it's <b>addictive</b>, I know that it's <b>flawless</b>. <br /><br />•<b>The main characters</b>, <b>Kate Harker</b> and <b>August Flynn</b>, are particularly easy to empathize with, my basis for comparison being Kell and Lila from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/122142" rel="nofollow noopener">Shades of Magic</a> trilogy and Vctor and Eli from <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>
</i>. Schwab's characters are always relatable, to a lesser or greater degree, but Kate and August appear to have something, a kind of <b>vulnerability</b>, I think, that makes them extremely <b>open</b>, exposed to the reader's eye, and thus to his heart. I was used to less decipherable personalities, more reserved minds, and although my favorite character of hers remains the frowning (and adorable) Kell, single-minded Kate and loyal August are so <b>well-rounded</b> I really have nothing to complain about. <br /><br />•<b>The monsters</b>. Suffice it to say this: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they are generated by great amounts of negativity, from lumps of nasty emotions <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />I am sold.<br />This (big) detail swept me off my feet. <br />And just like that, even without mentioning the divided city, the system by which it's run and a million other things, the <b>world building</b> gets a five out of five. <br /><br />•According to what Victoria herself stated, "books published under V.E. Schwab are <b>adult releases</b> and those under Victoria Schwab are <b>YA</b>", which means that <i>This Savage Song</i> is my first YA written by her. (I know, I'll get <i>The Archived</i> sooner than soon.) I noticed the differences with the adult releases, and probably that's the reason why the book didn't reach a full five for me. I just think that books such as <i>Vicious</i> and the Shades have something that makes them superior, even though I am not one hundred percent sure it is due to the different target.<br /><br />•<b>The ending</b> I refuse to acknowledge because even though it's not a real cliffhanger <i>I need to know what happens next</i>. <i>I needed it like yesterday</i>. <i>I think it made me a little hysterical</i>. *internally screaming*<br /><br />➽ The only reason the last star is missing is that Schwab spoiled me with her other books. <b>I am a spoiled reader because of this woman</b> and I have no regrets. I'll just need to hibernate until book 2 is out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16952691068445638473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13224495313558413038">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>this savage song is a book i was really excited to start because of all the hype surrounding it. it was apparently badass and had a cool idea of monsters, humans and evil. what i got was?? much less terrifying and made me laugh out loud because what the fuck, these whiny monsters were supposed to be scary??? it's like that ghost gif where you're waiting for that creepy jump scare but what you get is a guy with a white sheet on him, going around saying "booo."<br/><br/>here are some pros:<br/>-i loved</span>
  <span id="freeText13224495313558413038" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />this savage song is a book i was really excited to start because of all the hype surrounding it. it was apparently badass and had a cool idea of monsters, humans and evil. what i got was?? much less terrifying and made me laugh out loud because what the fuck, these whiny monsters were supposed to be scary??? it's like that ghost gif where you're waiting for that creepy jump scare but what you get is a guy with a white sheet on him, going around saying "booo."<br /><br />here are some pros:<br />-i loved how Schwab has non existent romance in her books. the relationship between August and Kate is well done. the way they develop from enemies to friends (not lovers) is also an amazing trope and should be used more often in books. <br /><br />-the writing is beautifully done and easy to read. while there was a hell of a slow and boring plot, the writing made it all easier and i legit flew through this book. the words just flow through you making the book a bit bearable. <br /><br />-ummmm, that's about it??<br /><br />cons:<br />-so, where the fuck is the world building. it seriously lacks that. <br /><br />-Kate was a character i didn't like at all. y'all this bitch pissed me off. i felt like Schwab just goes over the top to make her female characters extremely badass. (first it was Lila with her annoying reckless behavior and now Kate.) ok so, being badass doesn't mean you threaten/hurt innocent people. that doesn't make you fucking badass but fucking psychotic and go find help??? thanks. while i admit burning down the chapel was cool, it was unnecessary??? why would you even fucking do that though, what if people got hurt?? oh but Kate Harker wouldn't give a fuck because she's badass like that, oh yeah! right, go fuck yourself. i'm sorry but her behavior pissed me off, like yo you need an ass whooping. <br /><br />ohhh not to mention her constant saying of "i'm Kate Harker" "i'm Harker's daughter" "people fear my father" "i'm much worse than my father"<br /><br />OK SCHWAB I GET IT, I CAN'T BE AS "BADASS" AND AS COOL AS HER, no need to shove how great she is down my throat every five pages??? please. thanks. <br /><br />so, overall, Kate Harker's a piece of shit. <br /><br />-i also didn't really like August that much. i don't really hate his character, but i don't particularly like him either. i don't know he comes off as like a dead zombie to me and i couldn't really care for him. <br /><br />-the plot. <br />what the fuck<br />it was so slow<br />and boring<br />nothing happens<br />literally nothing exciting happened until the last couple of chapter which left me so fucking bored and uninterested in the entire story. the idea of it was really cool, but executed poorly. <br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">daddy</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/46651661-solomon-the-bookish-king" rel="nofollow noopener">mr. Thicc</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1449202895" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449202895" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1449202895?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062380876" href="/book/show/23299512-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=pnr-uf">pnr-uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449202895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3256407006633770456"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468201003i/19677567._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Buddy-read with the ever amazing Hufflepuff, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640655451?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chelsea</a> (click to read her review)</i><br/><br/><b><u>3.5/4 stars</u>.</b> So. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_' title='This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Savage Song</a>. <b>Rarely a novel created so many divergent reactions in my feed</b>. If the fact that opinions differ doesn't strike me as unusual - suffice it to take a look at most romance novels' pages to see radically different ratings - it still contributed to my confusion before reading because mixing most of them would lead to a hell of an oxymoron. <br/><br/>The world-building is fantastic and original, <i>but</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3256407006633770456" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468201003i/19677567._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Buddy-read with the ever amazing Hufflepuff, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640655451?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a> (click to read her review)</i><br><br><b><u>3.5/4 stars</u>.</b> So. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a>. <b>Rarely a novel created so many divergent reactions in my feed</b>. If the fact that opinions differ doesn't strike me as unusual - suffice it to take a look at most romance novels' pages to see radically different ratings - it still contributed to my confusion before reading because mixing most of them would lead to a hell of an oxymoron. <br><br>The world-building is fantastic and original, <i>but generic.</i> <br>The characters are well-rounded and complex, <i>but rather dull and one-dimensional</i>. <br>It was unputdownable. <i>It was so fucking boring</i>.<br>It lacked romance. <i>Thanks god there's no romance</i>. <br><br>I very much enjoyed reading all these interesting and well-thought reviews - and I am not being ironic - yet my questions started piling up with increasing speed : so, what? <b>Would <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> be the first novel from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> that would leave me indifferent?</b> Should I lower my expectations? Would I like, would I like, would I like? <br><br>But then I thought : <b>Anna, these reviews aren't about you</b>. Such a tiny thing, this. So easily forgotten. As much as we start noticing similarities between our tastes and particular reviewers' over the years, their reviews are never, ever, about ourselves. How could they? <br><br>I guess that's why it baffles me so much when I see people leaving hmm, let's say, <i>tactless</i> comments on reviews they don't agree with. Sure, sometimes we can't change the facts. Does the MC cheat? Is there consent? (because yes, I'm one of these people who think that there's nothing grey or "blurred" about consent) But most of the words written in a review are opinions and are linked to so many factors : the number of books read in that genre, the personal tastes, the current mood, etc, etc. <br><br>We can organize our reviews all we want, use bullet points or dialectical reasoning, who cares, it doesn't change a thing (or ramble before even talking about the book itself, I know, I know, the irony isn't left on me). <br><br>In the end, <b>sometimes our opinion will only revolve around the chemistry we share with a particular author and her work</b>. This is where I stand when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> is concerned. <br><br>Does that mean that I will love every one of her books? Hell no. I only liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23299512.This_Savage_Song__Monsters_of_Verity___1_" title="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a> awoke the same kind of contradictory feelings in me : <br><br>✔ As usual with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a>'s novels, I was <b>fascinated by the concept</b> and the writing managed (without forcing, it seems) to tug at my heartstrings at the most random moments. <br><br>✘ ✔ The pacing didn't suit me during the first 50%, my read was interspersed by at least 10 minutes of rest every few chapters, but <b>once the second half started, the story captivated me so much</b> that I forgot everything that wasn't August (yes. I am playing favorites) - <i>it started with a whimper, ended with a bang?</i> How fitting. <br><br>✔ <b>Verity's monsters were as disturbing as engrossing to read about</b>, and the darkness lurking enveloped me completely. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Be careful, parents told their children, be good, or the Corsai will come, but the truth was the Corsai didn't care if you were careful or good. They swam in darkness and fed on fear, their bodies sick, distended shapes that looked human only if you caught them out of the corner of your eye."</b>
</blockquote><br>✘ The somewhat dystopian settings made me think that really, I'm not sure we need to read about <b>a umpteenth version of the decaying United States</b>. I'd rather go somewhere else next time. Really. Please think about it.<br><br>✘ ✔ I would say that the characters are <b>pretty generic and trope-ish</b>, because this is what my mind was screaming at first, but I cannot dismiss the fact that they made me care and snort and bite my nails and <i>feel</i>. They left me craving for <i>more</i>. <b>Perhaps <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> used an old mold to craft her characters, it doesn't change the fact that they genuinely interested me and that I, for one, enjoyed their dynamics a lot</b>. <br><br>Also, I really have a thing for male leads who sob and whisper. I KNOW. THIS IS RIDICULOUS. But THIS IS WHO I AM. It only works in books, though. Weird how attraction works, ha. In real life I would probably say something along the lines of, [frowns] why the hell are you whispering?! Because of course. Kill Mood Is Me. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"This was the opposite of peace. He felt alive – so alive – but tarnished, his sense screaming and his head a tangle of dark thoughts and feelings and power, and he was drowning and shivering and burning alive."</b>
</blockquote><br>► My review, it seems, is everything but helpful. This being said, given the huge fanbase <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> has - which she deserves, as far as I'm concerned - I know that my review will hardly change anything in your decision. Read it, don't read it. <u>One thing is sure</u> : your review will be unique and genuinely interesting to me. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3256407006633770456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703227502?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062380876" href="/book/show/23299512-this-savage-song">review of another edition</a>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703227502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7090873395077481203"><i> “It's a monster's world.”</i><br/><br/>Idk how to write a review for this book. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500400758i/23334573._SY540_.png' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a href='http://puali.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>(s)</a> <br/><s>my schwab and 21 pilats heart is overwhelmed to see this</s><br/><br/>Schwab has proved herself to me time and time again. I’m legitimately so trash for her that if she published her shopping list, I would just //become// <i>Incoherent Scream</i> and bounce around shoving it in the faces of strangers. <br/>I know, it doesn’t sound very healthy. <br/><br/><b>AUGUST FLYNN IS MY PRECIOUS LITTLE EMO BABY I WOULD DIE FOR HIM DON’T FRICKEN TOUCH ME</b><br/><br/>This book had a lot of</span>
  <span id="freeText7090873395077481203" style="display:none"><i> “It's a monster's world.”</i><br><br>Idk how to write a review for this book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500400758i/23334573._SY540_.png" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://puali.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">(s)</a> <br><s>my schwab and 21 pilats heart is overwhelmed to see this</s><br><br>Schwab has proved herself to me time and time again. I’m legitimately so trash for her that if she published her shopping list, I would just //become// <i>Incoherent Scream</i> and bounce around shoving it in the faces of strangers. <br>I know, it doesn’t sound very healthy. <br><br><b>AUGUST FLYNN IS MY PRECIOUS LITTLE EMO BABY I WOULD DIE FOR HIM DON’T FRICKEN TOUCH ME</b><br><br>This book had a lot of things I //didn’t// expect to like mainly <i>vampires</i> but damn man, Schwab knows how to USE those tropes !!<br><br>Also there was no romance which was WHOA for a YA book but also incredibly refreshing but you know what, my shipper heart doesn’t EFFING CARE BC I STILL SHIPPED AND IM READY TO DIE FOR THESE KIDS<br><br>I’m kinda in love with the trope of <i>forbidden love</i> so :) :) :) this better happen Schwab :) :) this better fricken happen :) :) :)<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500400758i/23334574._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://thaneasty.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">(s)</a> <br><br>We’ll do a quick list of Thoughts:<br>-	Isla is an angel<br>-	So is August<br>-	Leo can choke<br>-	@ Henry and Emily FRICKEN ADOPT ME<br>-	Kate’s dad can choke<br>-	Kate is a walking cliché but she’s kinda won me over<br>-	I want Schwab’s quotes to be printed on a shirt so I can walk around and everyone will know my true form<br>-	If august gets hurt in book 2 im gonna fricken sue<br>-	Has he not suffered enough in book 1???????<br><br>The only reason this <i>isn’t</i> 5 stars is bc it lagged in the beginning and it was kinda tropey but im still trash take your judgment away from me<br><br>Anyways<br>That’s all<br>I just want to start the next book<br><br><i> “It was a cruel trick of the universe, thought August, that he only felt human after doing something monstrous.”</i><br><br>4 stars!!<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><b>
  <i>Fake buddy read</i>
</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61624004" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily</a><br><br>im here so i can complete my title of Schwab Trash™ and wear it like a badge of honour</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ayEwDuqR/DCT3JRwv7pa44U4E8aMz26OmnmD/WKt35bdd80xNolUrWc3f6XX9nGm9i2qjnNZp1i7qlnKMdIg1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7jk4iFKh3XFNIq2ACkz9BqT/MXUNuSAXkP6qA2R8j7BYb8W3jrl17LnJRlViANZD1+qIPfIv6cGxLXA0NwNw8g==')})
  }
